**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:
Breaking political news
Opinion pieces and editorials
Legislation and policy discussions
Elections, political figures, and government actions

It's moderated to focus on U.S.-centric content and generally avoids memes or low-effort posts. The subreddit can have a progressive or liberal-leaning tone, depending on the community's engagement, though it hosts a range of political perspectives.

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. **Summary of Revisions:**

1.  **Elevated Immigration to a Standalone Area:** My initial structure combined immigration with other executive branch actions. Upon review, the volume and specificity of news concerning immigration and border security—including asylum policy, legal challenges, enforcement, and rhetoric—warranted its own top-level category (Area 3). This gives the topic the prominence it deserves based on the news cycle.
2.  **Refined Executive Branch Category:** By moving immigration to its own area, Area 2 ("Executive Branch") is now more coherently focused on the administration's internal operations, management of federal agencies (like USAID, NOAA, FBI HQ), presidential conduct (the Paramount settlement, Oval Office meetings), and personnel decisions. I also added a specific topic for "Legal Scrutiny and Investigations" to house stories about calls for probes into the administration or related figures.
3.  **Clarified Judicial vs. Executive Actions:** The new structure better distinguishes between different branches of government. For instance, legal challenges to the administration's asylum policy are now logically grouped under the "Immigration" area (Topic 3.1), while cases directly before or petitioned to the Supreme Court on other matters are in the "Judicial" area (Topic 6.1). This prevents confusing overlaps.
4.  **Improved Topic Wording:** I have refined the wording of several topics for greater precision. For example, "Federal Asylum Policy and Legal Challenges" is more specific than a general "Policy" topic. "State/Local Races and Key Political Figures" better captures the focus on individuals like Zohran Mamdani.

I believe this revised six-area structure is more robust, logical, and ultimately more useful for the intended audience.

Choosing your length appropriately by importance and complexity of that topic. You should learn from all the headlines, and especially the ones with high importance scores under the topic, discover their connections, and put everything into a coherent narrative, and provide citations (the IDs of news articles) for your claims. You need to cover the main ideas behind all the articles, but you don't need to cite every single of them. You only cite the meaningful, high-quality sources. You should never use overly broad, generic phrasing, which is a mistake you often make. Keep tone urgent, stick to the facts, use concrete examples, be razor sharp, be non-partisan. Do not offer policy recommendations. No editorializing or speculation — stick strictly to facts in the JSON. Sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. In that case, keep to what the headlines explicitly say, and explain that information is insufficient, and keep the summary brief. Do not make your own guesses to fill up the space!

**Please be super aware of the possibility of hallucinations!** That is absolutely not allowed. This is a common problem for LLMs like you. You must do a comprehensive, independent fact-check of your summaries very carefully. Every name, job title, date, event, quote, and other facts should be exactly as what you learned from the news headlines. Be fully aware that your internal knowledge base is outdated.

Composing: 

Consider that our overall length of the document should be **1300-1700 words**, **not counting the URLs if they are present**, you may need to adjust the length of each area and topic, and you may need to skip or merge topics or areas, if there is no enough space for the original version. If you skipped or merged topics or areas, you should also re-order the headers of areas and topics accordingly. On the other hand, sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. In that case, keep to what the headlines explicitly say, and explain that information is insufficient, and keep the summary brief. Do not make your own guesses to fill up the space!

### **Area 1: The "Big, Beautiful Bill" - Central Legislative Battle**

**Topic 1.1: Congressional Vote and Legislative Maneuvering**

The primary legislative focus on Capitol Hill is a sweeping piece of legislation, referred to as the "big, beautiful bill," which now faces a critical and uncertain vote in the House of Representatives. Republican leadership is conducting a "last-ditch megabill whip job," which includes President Trump personally meeting with House GOP factions to shore up support [1]. Despite these efforts, the bill's outcome remains in jeopardy due to staunch opposition from a bloc of Republican "hard-liners" [1]. The urgency of the situation is underscored by reports of House members rushing back to Washington specifically for this vote [2]. This legislative push follows the Senate's passage of its own version of the bill, the impacts of which are already causing states like New York to prepare for significant changes [3].

**Topic 1.2: Impact on Healthcare and Social Programs**

Key provisions within the legislation are reported to have severe consequences for public health and social safety nets. Analyses project that millions of Americans could lose their health insurance coverage [1], and the bill is described as being designed to "decimate Medicaid" in a way that will be "unspeakably cruel" for certain groups [2]. The debate has a tangible human element, with Representative Adam Schiff publicly shaming Senate Republicans for voting against an amendment that would have protected children's food assistance programs, calling the vote "'just awful'" [3]. Projections also suggest the negative health impacts will disproportionately harm rural communities [4].

The administration's rhetoric on immigration remains severe. President Trump has renewed a "chilling call to deport US-born offenders" with the phrase "Get Them the Hell Out" [1]. This is defended by Secretary of Homeland Security Kristi Noem, who stated the President is "upholding freedom by deporting cannibals" [2]. Meanwhile, a proposed detention center in the Everglades, dubbed "Alligator Alcatraz," is reportedly already flooding [3]. The proposal has spawned inflammatory rhetoric, with a Trump ally reportedly suggesting alligators are "'guaranteed at least 65 million meals'" and a MAGA influencer hinting at feeding immigrants to gators [4].

## 4. Foreign Policy and National Security
### 4.1 Halt to Ukraine Arms Shipments and Global Security
A sudden and significant shift in U.S. policy toward Ukraine has occurred. The administration has halted all arms shipments to the country, a decision that has reportedly caught European partners "off guard" [1]. This abrupt stop in U.S. military supply has directly led to fears within Ukraine of increased Russian aggression and is forcing Kyiv to urgently pursue joint weapons production initiatives with its remaining allies [2]. In the Middle East, reports indicate American contractors in Gaza have witnessed colleagues firing "live ammo" at Palestinians seeking food [3]. A new proposal suggests President Trump could arm Israel with advanced U.S. B-2s and bunker-buster munitions if Iran moves to develop nuclear weapons [4]. In a separate development, President Trump has announced a new trade deal between the United States and Vietnam [5].

## 5. Domestic Politics and Elections
### 5.1 Party Politics, Elections, and Potential Realignment
President Trump is now directly involved in the New York City mayor's race, publicly making the false claim that candidate Zohran Mamdani is an illegal immigrant and threatening his arrest [1]. Elsewhere, a new poll identifies former Vice President Kamala Harris as a favorite in the California governor's race, should she choose to run [2]. Simultaneously, speculation about a major political realignment is growing. Reports detail "secret talks" between Republican and Democratic factions to create a new third party [3], while the Libertarian party is actively seeking a partnership with Elon Musk [4], whose own proposed "America Party" is being analyzed for its potential to act as a spoiler to the GOP [5]. Commentary suggests President Trump is beginning the summer "on a hot streak," with one report claiming news giants like CBS are "bending to Trump's power" [6].

## 6. Judicial and State-Level Developments
### 6.1 Divergent State Policies on Civil Rights and Abortion
State courts and legislatures are creating sharply divergent policy landscapes. The Wisconsin Supreme Court has struck down the state's 1849-era abortion ban, a major victory for abortion rights advocates [1]. In a starkly contrasting move, Iowa's government has become the first in the nation to remove "gender identity" from its civil rights code, thereby legally permitting anti-transgender discrimination [2]. In Wyoming, a new law requiring age verification on adult websites has taken effect, drawing comment from the porn industry and the Supreme Court [3]. The state's governor has also appointed a former state Supreme Court justice who has publicly spoken out against abortion as the new attorney general [4].

[3] Porn industry, Supreme Court weigh in as Wyoming requires age verification on adult sites, https://wyofile.com/porn-industry-supreme-court-weigh-in-as-wyoming-requires-age-verification-on-adult-sites/

### 6.2 Supreme Court Actions and Major Criminal Cases
The Executive Branch has petitioned the U.S. Supreme Court to remove three Democratic members from the Consumer Product Safety Commission [1]. In the criminal justice sphere, a jarring case has concluded: a Jan. 6 rioter, who had received a presidential pardon for his role in the riot, was subsequently sentenced to life in prison for plotting to murder the FBI agents who had investigated him [2, 3]. Separately, the FBI has announced the uncovering of what it describes as the "largest medical fraud in US history" [4].
